The provided article discusses the various opinions and ideas of different political parties in the UK regarding apprenticeships. To summarize the article based on the given requirement, the following is an appropriate summary:  "The UK's main political parties are emphasizing the importance of apprenticeships as a solution to youth unemployment and a means for career qualification. The Conservatives aim to create 16,000 new apprenticeships and consider them on par with degrees. Labour pledges to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, particularly through the High Speed 2 rail line project. The Liberal Democrats seek to expand apprenticeships and vocational skills through national colleges. UKIP proposes allowing students to take apprenticeships instead of certain GCSE subjects. The Green Party plans to increase funding for apprenticeships, while the SNP aims to provide 125,000 modern apprenticeships. Plaid Cymru supports the European Union's Youth Jobs Guarantee and higher-level apprenticeships."  Now, let's evaluate the two assistants' answers:  <|The Start of Answer (a)|> The main political parties in the UK are all pushing for more apprenticeships to help young people find work and gain qualifications. The Conservatives have proposed creating 16,000 new apprenticeships, with a promise to create an extra three million 'training places' if the party remains in power after the general election in May. They want to pay for it with money saved from benefits caps. Baroness Brady, a Tory peer and star of The Apprentice (fittingly enough), said the party wants apprenticeships to be held on par with degrees. Labour has pledged to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, with 33,000 of those coming from the High Speed 2 rail line. The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills, while UKIP has proposed an option for students to take an apprenticeship instead of four non-core GCSE subjects. The Green Party has promised to expand apprenticeships by increasing funding, while the SNP has pledged to provide 125,000 modern apprenticeships and Plaid Cymru wants to promote higher level apprenticeships and in-work learning. <|The End of Answer (a)|>  <|The Start of Answer (b)|> The article discusses the opinions and ideas of different people regarding apprenticeships. The Conservatives want to create 16,000 new apprenticeships, with a promise to create an extra three million 'training places' if the party remains in power after the general election in May. They want to pay for it with money saved from benefits caps. Baroness Brady, a Tory peer and star of The Apprentice (fittingly enough), said the party wants apprenticeships to be held on par with degrees. Labour has pledged to create 80,000 more apprenticeships. However, 33,000 of those would come from just one project, the High Speed 2 rail line (HS2). That raises questions about what will happen once that project is complete, or if it suffers any delays. Ed Miliband has promised apprenticeships to every school leaver who "gets the grades" - that's level 3 qualifications, which are equivalent to having two A-levels. Those with two A-Levels will also qualify, but the scheme will exclude those who only have GCSEs. The party has also announced plans to boost job prospects for young people by giving teenagers face-to-face advice in schools. That will include steering people towards more apprenticeships, rather than directing them towards university or unskilled jobs. The scheme has been budgeted at £50m. Nick Clegg has pledged to expand apprenticeships and develop national colleges for vocational skills. He wants to end the "barely concealed snobbery" about apprenticeships, which he claims comes from adults, rather than young people. The Lib Dems have gone to great lengths to point out the two million apprenticeships available under the coalition, stating that he and Vince Cable have been instrumental in pushing for them. The party told Newsbeat it wants to double that number in the next parliament. UKIP has pledged to introduce an option for students to take an apprenticeship (with a qualification at the end) instead of four non-core GCSE subjects. The employers they work with will be qualified to test and grade the apprentices, and the students can carry on working with them through their A-levels. The party has also promised to scrap the target of 50% of school leavers going on to university, while scrapping tuition fees for some students taking degrees in high-demand vocational subjects like maths, technology, engineering, medicine and science - so long as they live, work and pay taxes in the UK for five years after they graduate. The Green Party hasn't published a specific policy on apprenticeships, but told News <|The End of Answer(b)|>  Evaluation: Answer (a) is concise and covers the main points of the article, including the proposals from the Conservatives, Labour, Liberal Democrats, UKIP, Green Party, SNP, and Plaid Cymru. It provides a clear summary of the different political parties
The provided article discusses the various opinions and ideas of different political parties in the UK regarding apprenticeships. To summarize the article based on the given requirement, the following summary would be appropriate:  The article highlights the various political parties' approaches to apprenticeships. The Conservatives aim to create 16,000 new apprenticeships and want to elevate their status to be on par with degrees. Labour pledges to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, particularly through the High Speed 2 rail line project, and to provide better careers advice. The Liberal Democrats plan to expand apprenticeships and establish national colleges for vocational skills. UKIP proposes allowing students to take apprenticeships instead of certain GCSE subjects and to scrap the target of 50% of school leavers going to university. The Green Party advocates for increased funding for apprenticeships and ensuring all qualified young people aged 16-25 have access to them. The SNP aims to provide 125,000 modern apprenticeships, focusing on high-tech industries, and Plaid Cymru supports the European Union's Youth Jobs Guarantee and higher-level apprenticeships. The article discusses the various opinions and ideas of different political parties in the UK regarding apprenticeships. Here is a summary based on the given requirement:  The Conservatives aim to create 16,000 new apprenticeships and three million training places, with a goal of holding apprenticeships on par with degrees. Labour plans to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, with a focus on the High Speed 2 rail line project and offering apprenticeships to school leavers with certain qualifications. The Liberal Democrats want to expand apprenticeships and vocational skills education, aiming to end the snobbery associated with apprenticeships. UKIP proposes allowing students to take an apprenticeship instead of certain GCSE subjects and scrapping tuition fees for vocational degrees. The Green Party plans to increase funding for apprenticeships and provide them to all qualified young people aged 16-25. The SNP aims to provide 125,000 modern apprenticeships and offer training schemes to unemployed or training 16 to 19-year-olds. Plaid Cymru supports the EU's Youth Jobs Guarantee and promotes higher level apprenticeships and in-work learning. The Start of My Answer: The article discusses various political parties' opinions and ideas regarding apprenticeships. The Conservatives aim to create 16,000 new apprenticeships and three million training places, with a goal of making apprenticeships equivalent to degrees. Labour plans to create 80,000 more apprenticeships, particularly through the High Speed 2 rail line project, and offers apprenticeships to school leavers with certain grades. The Liberal Democrats focus on expanding apprenticeships and vocational colleges, aiming to reduce the stigma associated with apprenticeships. UKIP proposes allowing students to take an apprenticeship instead of certain GCSE subjects and scrapping tuition fees for vocational degrees. The Green Party seeks to expand apprenticeships through increased funding and ensure all qualified young people aged 16-25 have access to an apprenticeship. The SNP plans to provide 125,000 modern apprenticeships and offer training schemes to unemployed or training 16 to 19-year-olds. Plaid Cymru supports the EU's Youth Jobs Guarantee and promotes higher-level apprenticeships and in-work learning. To summarize the differences in the definition of collusion provided by these individuals:  1. **Lord Stevens**: Collusion ranges from the wilful failure to keep records, the absence of accountability, the withholding of intelligence and evidence, to the extreme of agents being involved in murder.  2. **Peter Cory**: Includes secret cooperation, turning a blind eye to wrongful acts, and emphasizes the necessity for public confidence in government agencies.  3. **Nuala O'Loan**: Adopted the definitions of Lord Stevens and Peter Cory to examine whether there had been collusion in specific cases.  4. **Al Hutchinson**: Applied a less broad definition, requiring an agreement between parties and sufficient evidence to establish deliberate acts or omissions.  5. **Sir Christopher de Silva**: Adopted a working definition similar to the Billy Wright inquiry panel, emphasizing that omissions must be deliberate and not merely examples of incompetence or inefficiency.  6. **Peter Smithwick**: Similar to Peter Cory, including both active acts and omissions or failures to act.  Now, let's evaluate the assistants' answers:  **Answer (a)**: This answer provides a concise summary of the different definitions of collusion. It mentions Lord Stevens, Peter Cory, Nuala O'Loan, Al Hutchinson, Sir Christopher de Silva, and Peter Smithwick, and highlights the key aspects of their definitions. The article discusses a case of fraud where a woman's mother, Margaret, had over £14,000 stolen through direct debit fraud. The daughter, Sue, was outraged and sought help from her mother's bank, Lloyds, and the company that the direct debits were being paid to, Vodafone. Both Lloyds and Vodafone initially denied any responsibility, stating that the direct debits had been "legitimately" set up. Sue also contacted her local police force and Action Fraud, but was told that no further action would be taken. Lloyds eventually agreed to refund the money stolen from Margaret's account, plus interest and compensation, after being contacted by the BBC. Vodafone also said it would provide the details of an individual who may have used Margaret's account to the police.  <|The Start of Answer (a)|> After being contacted by BBC Money Box, Lloyds started a new investigation and concluded that its initial response was wrong. They agreed to refund all of Margaret's money, plus interest and £600 by way of compensation. Vodafone also said they would provide the details of an individual who may have used Margaret's account to the police. Sue is grateful for the refund but hopes that someone will be held accountable for the fraud. <|The End of Answer (a)|>  <|The Start of Answer (b)|> The article discusses a case of fraud where a woman's mother had over 14,000 pounds stolen from her through direct debit fraud. The daughter, Sue, was outraged and contacted her mother's bank, Lloyds, and the company that the direct debits were being paid to, Vodafone. Both Lloyds and Vodafone told her that there was nothing they could do and that the direct debits had been "legitimately" set up. Sue then contacted her local police force and Action Fraud, but was told that it was unlikely any further action would be taken. Lloyds eventually agreed to refund the money stolen from Margaret's account, plus interest and compensation, after being contacted by the BBC. Vodafone said that it was also looking into the case and would provide the details of an individual who may have used Margaret's account to the police. <|The End of Answer(b)|>  # Decision: Both Answer (a) and Answer (b) provide a summary of the conclusion of the fraud case, including the key points of Lloyds' refund, Vodafone's involvement, and Sue's hope for accountability. However, Answer (a) is more concise and directly addresses the user's prompt by summarizing the conclusion without unnecessary details. Therefore, Answer (a) is better.
The article discusses a case of fraud where a woman's mother had over 14,000 pounds stolen from her through direct debit fraud. The daughter, Sue, was outraged and contacted her mother's bank, Lloyds, and the company that the direct debits were being paid to, Vodafone. Both Lloyds and Vodafone told her that there was nothing they could do and that the direct debits had been "legitimately" set up. Sue then contacted her local police force and Action Fraud, but was told that it was unlikely any further action would be taken. Vodafone said that it was also looking again at the case and would provide the details of an individual who may have used Margaret's account to the police. Some crew members have been moved to tears, particularly when they saw their images appear from the chemicals. To summarize Jack Lowe's background and his passion for photography and lifeboats based on the article:  Jack Lowe is a lifeboat enthusiast and photographer who has dedicated himself to recording the country's RNLI volunteers using Victorian photographic methods. He has a deep-seated passion for both photography and lifeboats, which was ignited at the age of 8. Lowe has abandoned his Newcastle printmaking business to embark on a journey around Britain's coast, photographing all 237 of the Royal National Lifeboat Institution's stations with a 110-year-old camera. He has converted an old ambulance into a darkroom to facilitate the Victorian photographic process, which is a time-consuming and meticulous process. Lowe is committed to giving the first print from each ambrotype to the station or crew member and plans to complete the project in four or five years. His ultimate goal is to become a lifeboatman himself.  Now, let's evaluate the assistants' answers:  Answer (a) provides a clear and concise summary of Jack Lowe's background and passion. It includes his lifelong love for photography and lifeboats, his decision to give up his business, his use of Victorian photographic methods, and his intention to become a lifeboatman. However, it omits some important information, such as Lowe's age, his conversion of an old ambulance into a darkroom, and his plan to become a lifeboatman. The Victorian photographic method used by Jack Lowe involves coating a glass plate with chemicals, exposing it to light through a camera, and then applying a fixative to set the image. This method produces an ambrotype, which is a positive image on glass. The process is time-sensitive, requiring the image to be developed within about 15 minutes. The exposure time can be up to 12 seconds, necessitating a willing subject and often an overcast location to ensure the image is clear. The camera's shutter must remain open for longer in low light conditions, which can be challenging for the photographer and the subject.  Now, let's evaluate the assistants' answers:  Answer (a) provides a clear and concise summary of the Victorian photographic method and the process Jack Lowe uses. It mentions the coating of the glass plate with chemicals, the exposure to light, and the application of a fixative. It also notes the time sensitivity of the process and the exposure time. However, it does not mention the use of a 110-year-old camera or the specific duration of the process (15 minutes).  Answer (b) includes all the key elements mentioned in Answer (a), but it adds additional details that are relevant to the prompt. It specifies that Jack Lowe uses a 110-year-old camera and that the process must be completed within 15 minutes. It also mentions the need for longer shutter exposure in low light conditions, which is an important aspect of the process.  Considering the completeness and accuracy of the information provided, Answer (b) is more detailed and informative. It includes all the necessary elements of the prompt and adds a layer of specificity that is helpful for understanding the process.  Therefore, Answer (b) is better.

The provided article outlines the evolution of American alcohol consumption, starting from the Puritan era to the present day. To summarize the changes in American alcohol consumption based on the given requirement, the following summary is appropriate:  In the early days of America, alcohol consumption was high, with an average of 5.8 gallons of pure alcohol consumed per person per year. By 1830, consumption had reached a peak of 7.1 gallons per year. The late 19th century saw the rise of alcoholism as a public health concern, leading to the Prohibition era in 1917. However, by the 1930s, the Great Depression prompted a shift in public opinion, leading to the repeal of Prohibition in 1933. Since then, alcohol consumption has decreased to an average of 2.3 gallons of pure alcohol per person per year.  Now, let's evaluate the assistants' answers:  Answer (a) is concise and directly addresses the requirement by summarizing the changes in American alcohol consumption over time. It provides a clear timeline of consumption levels and the impact of Prohibition.  Answer (b) is more detailed and includes additional historical context, such as the Puritans' views on alcohol and the role of alcohol in American culture. However, it does not as directly or concisely summarize the changes in alcohol consumption as Answer (a).  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.
The article discusses the history of alcohol consumption in America, highlighting the changes over time. The Puritans, initially thought to be against alcohol, were actually approving of it. Consumption was high in the 18th and early 19th centuries, with an average of 5.8 gallons of pure alcohol consumed per person per year in 1790. This began to decline as alcoholism became a recognized issue in the 1830s, leading to the peak consumption of 7.1 gallons in 1830. Prohibition was introduced in 1917 but was eventually repealed in 1933, and today, Americans consume an average of 2.3 gallons of pure alcohol per year.  Answer (a) is more concise and directly addresses the changes in American alcohol consumption. It mentions the Puritans' stance on alcohol, the peak consumption, the introduction of Prohibition, and the current consumption rate. It also briefly touches on the role of the presidency in rehabilitating alcohol, which is relevant to the topic.  Answer (b) is more detailed and includes additional information about the rise of speakeasies and organized crime during Prohibition, which is not directly related to the summary requirement. While this information is interesting, it is not necessary for summarizing the changes in American alcohol consumption.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.

To summarize the symptoms of prosopagnosia based on the given article:  Prosopagnosia is a condition characterized by the inability to recognize faces, despite the ability to see individual facial features such as the eyes, nose, and mouth. Individuals with prosopagnosia often struggle to identify gestures and emotions, and may not be able to recognize even close friends or family members if they are not expecting to see them. The condition can result from birth defects or brain injuries and currently has no cure. People with prosopagnosia may develop coping strategies, but these are not always reliable.  Now, let's evaluate the assistants' answers:  Answer (a) provides a comprehensive summary of the symptoms of prosopagnosia, including the inability to recognize faces, the difficulty in perceiving gestures and emotions, and the potential for not recognizing familiar individuals if they are not anticipated. It also mentions the causes of the condition and the lack of a cure, which are relevant to the user prompt. The answer is concise and clear.  Answer (b) is also concise and mentions the main symptoms of prosopagnosia, such as the difficulty in recognizing faces and the inability to see the whole face. However, it does not include information about the inability to recognize gestures or emotions, which is an important aspect of the condition. It also omits the causes and the lack of a cure, which are relevant details.  Considering the completeness and accuracy of the information provided, Answer (a) is more thorough and informative. It includes all the key symptoms and relevant details about the condition, making it a more helpful and relevant response.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.
To summarize the symptoms of prosopagnosia based on the given article:  Prosopagnosia is a condition characterized by the inability to recognize faces, even of familiar individuals. Individuals with prosopagnosia can see the individual features of a face, such as the eyes, nose, and mouth, but they cannot integrate these features into a coherent whole. This results in difficulty in recognizing the person as a whole, and they often fail to recognize gestures or emotions. There are two main types of prosopagnosia: developmental, which is present from birth and affects approximately 2% of the population, and acquired, which is caused by brain injury and is much rarer. To summarize the article based on the given requirement, the role of UNICEF in India's polio eradication efforts can be summarized as follows:  UNICEF has been instrumental in India's polio eradication campaign. It has provided financial and technical support to the National Polio Surveillance Project (NPSP), which is a collaboration between the Indian government and the World Health Organization (WHO). UNICEF established the Social Mobilisation Network for polio in 2001 in Uttar Pradesh to address resistance to the polio vaccine. The network worked to promote acceptance of the vaccine by focusing on community mobilization and addressing misconceptions. UNICEF also collaborated with various stakeholders, including the government, Rotary clubs, WHO, and front-line workers, to implement innovative strategies and micro-plans to ensure comprehensive vaccination coverage. It also highlights the implementation of innovative strategies and micro-plans, which were not mentioned in Answer (a).  Considering the completeness and accuracy of the information provided, Answer (b) is more helpful, relevant, and concise. The opening line-ups of the Home centre are summarized as follows:  1. The opening line-up of Manchester's new £25m arts centre Home includes Stockport playwright Simon Stephens' adaptation of Hungarian writer Odon von Horvath's 1932 play Kasimir and Karoline, renamed as The Funfair, and an art exhibition inspired by the play featuring artists from Egypt, Iceland, Kosovo, and Manchester. The opening line-ups are expected to provide more space to cater for Manchester's "hunger for new ideas" and to boost the economy by attracting other businesses to its part of the city centre.  2. The opening line-up for the new Home arts centre in Manchester includes a play by Stockport playwright Simon Stephens, an exhibition inspired by Hungarian writer Odon von Horvath's 1932 play Kasimir and Karoline, and screenings of funfair-themed films. The centre is hoped to boost the economy by attracting other businesses to its part of the city centre, and its artistic directors say it is an example of how arts can be a catalyst for regeneration. The campaign aims to challenge the over-testing culture and the impact of the tests on children's education. A social media campaign was launched to encourage parents to take their children on educational activities for the day. 500 people, including children's laureate Chris Riddell, gathered at Preston Park in Brighton to support the Let Our Kids Be Kids campaign. The petition was handed in at the Department for Education in London. The campaign organisers have raised concerns about the impact of primary tests and have challenged what they claim is a "dull, dry curriculum" based around tests. Education Minister Nick Gibb and Ofsted chief Sir Michael Wilshaw have argued that tests improve standards and need not be stressful. Chris McGovern, chairman of the Campaign for Real Education, has said that any short-term stress is worth it if it means that children finish school with better results.  **Answer (b):** Parents have kept their children out of school to protest against primary tests in England. They have complained of a damaging culture of over-testing and have called for a boycott of the tests. Education Secretary Nicky Morgan has said that taking pupils out of school for the day is harmful to their education. It remains uncertain how many primary school children were kept off school, but a social media campaign had urged parents to take their children on educational activities for the day. Therefore, Answer (a) is better.

Based on the given requirement to summarize the potential advantages of quantum computers compared to conventional computers, here is my own summary:  Quantum computers offer significant advantages over conventional computers due to their use of qubits, which can be in multiple states simultaneously and can communicate with each other over long distances. This allows them to perform complex calculations exponentially faster, making them ideal for tasks like cryptography, material science, and climate modeling. The Staffordshire Hoard has revealed that the Anglo-Saxons were highly skilled and technically advanced smiths, capable of producing intricate and delicate items. The hoard, which contains items mainly made of gold and silver, sometimes decorated with garnets, was believed to have been crafted in workshops in what is now England, with the garnets imported from Sri Lanka or India. The quality of the items has surprised researchers, as the majority were likely made for kings and their elite warriors. This discovery provides archaeological evidence of the elite warriors mentioned in poems such as Beowulf, which were previously thought to be fictional.  In comparing the two assistants' answers, both provide accurate summaries of the key points from the article. Answer (a) is concise and directly addresses the prompt by summarizing what the Staffordshire Hoard has taught us about the Anglo-Saxons. It mentions the skill of the smiths, the materials used, and the significance of the hoard in providing evidence of elite warriors.  Answer (b) also provides a good summary but includes additional information about the percentage of Anglo-Saxon items and the overall scale of the hoard compared to previous knowledge. This extra detail is relevant but may be considered slightly extraneous to the direct prompt, which asks for what the hoard has taught us about the Anglo-Saxons.  Given the prompt's focus on summarizing what the hoard has taught us, Answer (a) is more directly aligned with the requirement and is therefore more concise and relevant to the prompt.  Therefore, Answer (a) is better.

The article discusses the Staffordshire Hoard, which has provided significant insights into the Anglo-Saxons. The hoard consists of nearly 4,000 items, revealing the skill of the Anglo-Saxon smiths, their ability to produce gold with alloys, and delicate embossed foil. The items were made in workshops in what is now England, with garnets possibly imported from Sri Lanka or India. The quality of the items suggests they were for kings and elite warriors, and the hoard has increased the number of known Anglo-Saxon artifacts. It also serves as archaeological proof of the elite warriors mentioned in poems like Beowulf. Canadian judge Peter Cory expanded on this by including dictionary definitions and synonyms like "connive," emphasizing deliberate ignoring or overlooking. Nuala (now Baroness) O'Loan, the first police ombudsman for Northern Ireland, adopted Stevens' and Cory's definitions. Al Hutchinson, her successor, applied a narrower definition. To summarize the key statistics regarding the fire staff's mental health issues mentioned in the article, the following summary would be appropriate:  "The number of UK fire and rescue staff on long-term sick leave due to mental illness has increased by nearly a third over the past six years, with the figure rising from 600 to 780. In London, this figure has doubled since 2011-12, with 103 staff taking mental health leave this year. In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff and 111 Northern Ireland fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave. Since 2011, at least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues. The Home Office has allocated an additional £1.5m for mental health support through the Mind's Blue Light Programme."  Now, let's evaluate the two assistants' answers:  **Answer (a):** The number of UK fire and rescue staff taking long-term sick leave due to mental illness has risen by nearly a third over the last six years, with 600 to 780 cases reported. In London, the figure has doubled since 2011-12, with 103 fire staff taking mental health leave this year, some after working at Grenfell Tower. In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff and 111 Northern Ireland fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave. At least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues since 2011. The Home Office has provided an additional £1.5m to pay for mental health support through Mind's Blue Light Programme.  **Answer (b):** The number of UK fire and rescue staff taking long-term sick leave due to mental illness has risen by nearly a third over the last six years, with the figure doubling in London since 2011-12. Data from two-thirds of fire services revealed that the number of firefighters and other staff taking long-term mental health leave rose from 600 to 780 over the last six years. At least 126 staff have left the service due to mental health issues since 2011. In 2016-17, 97 Scottish fire staff took long-term mental health sick leave, while in Northern Ireland that figure was 111. A survey of over 1,600 staff and volunteers across emergency services shows nearly nine in 10 have experienced stress, low mood or poor mental health while working in their current role, and 25% of them had contemplated suicide.  Both answers (a) and (b) are helpful and relevant as they correctly summarize the key statistics regarding the fire staff's mental health issues. They are concise and provide the necessary information to understand the situation. However, Answer (b) includes an additional relevant statistic from a survey of over 1,600 staff and volunteers across emergency services, which adds depth to the summary. Therefore, it provides more comprehensive information.  **Therefore, Answer (b) is better.**

Based on the given requirement to summarize the quoted persons and their views, here is my own summary:  Dr. Sunil Shah of St George's at the University of London discusses a study that found a doubled risk of heart attacks or strokes in the month following a loved one's death compared to a non-grieving control group. The British Heart Foundation defines "broken heart syndrome" as a temporary condition where the heart muscle weakens or becomes stunned due to shock, often from bereavement or other significant stress. They differentiate this from heart attacks, which are typically caused by blockages and blood clots.
